import torch
import torch.nn as nn

class Model(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self):
        super(Model, self).__init__()

    def forward(self, Q: torch.Tensor, K: torch.Tensor, V: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
        out = torch.nn.functional.scaled_dot_product_attention(Q, K, V)
        return out

batch_size = 32
num_heads = 32
sequence_length = 512
embedding_dimension = 1024

def get_inputs():
    Q = torch.rand(batch_size, num_heads, sequence_length, embedding_dimension)
    K = torch.rand(batch_size, num_heads, sequence_length, embedding_dimension)
    V = torch.rand(batch_size, num_heads, sequence_length, embedding_dimension)
    return [Q, K, V]

def get_init_inputs():
    return []

The reference code says: ```python Q = torch.rand(batch_size, num_heads, sequence_length, embedding_dimension) ``` In standard multi-head attention, the last dimension should be `embedding_dimension // num_heads = 1024 // 32 = 32`. The MATH backend in PyTorch does: ```python attn_mask = None L, S = Q.size(-2), K.size(-2) scale_factor = 1 / math.sqrt(Q.size(-1)) attn_weight = Q @ K.transpose(-2, -1) * scale_factor attn_weight = torch.softmax(attn_weight, dim=-1) attn_weight = torch.dropout(attn_weight, dropout_p, train) output = attn_weight @ V ``` This calls `bmm` twice and `softmax`. For FP32, `bmm` calls cuBLAS strided batched GEMM. The intermediate `attn_weight` is materialized in HBM. Is it possible to write a better kernel? Maybe yes, if we fuse the entire thing. The second GEMM's M=512,N=1024,K=512. These are somewhat small inner dimensions. Total HBM traffic: read Q(2GB), K(2GB) -> compute S -> write S(1GB). Read S -> compute softmax -> write P(1GB). Read P, V(2GB) -> compute O -> write O(2GB). Total = ~10GB if we count unique. Each thread can compute one complete output element O[b,h,q,d]. To compute O[b,h,q,d], a thread needs: - Q[b,h,q,d] (float) - K[b,h,:,d] (512 floats) - V[b,h,:,d] (512 floats) (after softmax weights) But to compute softmax weight for key j, the thread needs dot(Q_q, K_j) which depends on all d. So a thread computing O[b,h,q,d] cannot compute softmax locally unless it knows all scores. So a thread block must compute all scores for its queries, then softmax, then compute all O for its queries. If one block per head handles all queries, it needs to compute the N x N score matrix (512x512 = 262k floats). This fits in registers/shared memory across threads (e.g., 256 threads * 1024 regs = 256k regs, but 262k floats * 4 bytes = 1MB. Actually 1024 threads * 255 registers = 261,120 registers. 512*512 = 262,144 floats. That's exactly one register per float. That's too tight and would leave no registers for other variables. Compiler would spill, causing terrible performance. We can use smaller number of threads and store S in shared memory. 512x512 = 262k floats = 1MB. A block has up to 48KB or with dynamic shared maybe 227KB max. So 1MB doesn't fit in shared memory. Therefore a single block cannot hold the entire S matrix in shared memory. It could compute S tile by tile and accumulate O. So the typical FlashAttention approach is necessary. But maybe we can choose a different parallelization: instead of one block per head, we can have blocks that handle a range of keys and do a reduction. This is similar to the "split-K" but with softmax. However, implementing the softmax reduction across blocks correctly is possible and not too complex if we use a two-pass or tree reduction. Specifically: - Partition keys into K_tiles (e.g., NK_blocks = 8). - Each block computes for all queries (or a query tile) and its key tile: - S_tile = Q[tile_q, :] @ K[key_tile, :]^T - local_max = max_j in key_tile S_tile - local_sum = sum_j exp(S_tile - local_max) - local_O = sum_j exp(S_tile - local_max) * V[key_tile, :] - Then we need to combine across key tiles for each query. We can use an atomic or a second reduction kernel. Paper: "Online normalizer calculation for softmax" (Milakov et al.) and "FlashAttention-2". The online softmax trick allows combining two chunks: Given chunk1 with m1, l1, o1; chunk2 with m2, l2, o2. m_new = max(m1, m2) l_new = exp(m1 - m_new) * l1 + exp(m2 - m_new) * l2 o_new = exp(m1 - m_new) * o1 + exp(m2 - m_new) * o2 So blocks can stream over key tiles and maintain running m, l, o. Within a single block, we can have it loop over key tiles. But the block still reads K and V for each key tile. If a block handles all queries, and loops over all key tiles, then K and V are read once. But the block would be very large (needs to handle 512 queries and 1024 features). The previous traffic analysis for the fused kernel assumed multiple query blocks per head, which caused K/V re-reads. With one block per head, we avoid re-reads. After `acc = acc + other`, both lanes have the full sum. This requires the `other` to come from lane k^16. - `float other = __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, acc, 16);` for lane k gets from lane k+16. For lane k+16, gets from k+32 (out of range => returns acc). So only lanes 0..15 get the sum. Let's just have lanes 0..15 store to smem. - `if (part == 0) acc = acc + __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, acc, 16);` // lane k gets lane k+16 value. - Then lane 0..15 writes acc to `s_smem[warp_id][key_k]`. This stores the full dot product for key_k. - After the dt loop, we have s_smem[q][k] for q=0..7, k=0..15. - Now we need max over k for each q. - For warp q: lanes 0..15 read s_smem[q][lane_id] (lane_id in 0..15). Lane 16..31 can also read or just idle. We need max over 16 values. - `float val = s_smem[warp_id][lane_id % 16];` - Warp reduce max over 32 lanes: we can do `for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) val = max(val, __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, val, offset));` - After this, lane 0 has m_tile (max over all 16 keys). - Next, compute l_tile = sum_k exp(s_k - m_tile). - `float val = expf(s_smem[warp_id][lane_id % 16] - m_tile);` - Warp reduce sum: `for offset... val += __shfl_down_sync(...)`. After, lane 0 has l_tile. - Next, compute p_k = exp(s_k - m_new) ... Actually we need to update running stats. - We have running m (per query) and running l (per query). These can be stored in registers for lane 0 of each warp. Or in shared memory (small array of 8 floats each). - m_new = max(m, m_tile). - correction_prev = expf(m - m_new); // if m was -inf, this is 0? Actually exp(-inf) = 0. - correction_tile = expf(m_tile - m_new); - l_new = correction_prev * l + correction_tile * l_tile; - // We also need p_k_raw = exp(s_k - m_new) for each key k. This is `exp(s_k - m_tile) * exp(m_tile - m_new) = exp(s_k - m_tile) * correction_tile`. - So for each key k, p_weight = exp(s_k - m_tile) * correction_tile. - We can store p_weight in `p_smem[q][k]` for k=0..15. Since p_smem is 8*16=128 floats. - Computation: lane_id in 0..15 reads s_smem[warp_id][lane_id], computes `p_weight = expf(s_k - m_tile) * correction_tile`. Writes to p_smem[warp_id][lane_id]. - Lane_id >= 16 can write to p_smem too if we want, but they don't have valid s. So only 0..15. - Then update O accumulator for this query group across all D tiles. - O accumulator: for each D tile, we have `o_acc[q][d]` in some memory. - We can store o_acc in shared memory: size = BQ * D = 8*1024 = 8192 floats = 32KB. This is exactly the O accumulator for the entire query group across all D dimensions. - Wait, we process query group once per key tile. Between key tiles, we need o_acc to persist. Smem is perfect for this. - Initialize o_acc to 0 before key tile loop. - For each key tile, after computing p_weights: - For each dt in 0..(D/DT - 1): - Load V[kt][dt] into v_smem[BK][DT] (16*64=1024 floats=4KB). - Threads update o_acc for their assigned d values. - Thread mapping for O update: - We need to compute for all q (8) and all d in dt (64) the update: `o_acc[q][dt*DT + d] = correction_prev * o_acc[q][...] + sum_k p_smem[q][k] * v_smem[k][d]`. - warp_id = q. - lane_id = 0..31. - For dt=64, each warp handles 64 d values. With 32 threads, each thread handles 2 d values: `d0 = lane_id`, `d1 = lane_id + 32`. - For each of its d values: - Compute local_sum = sum_{k=0}^{BK-1} p_smem[q][k] * v_smem[k][d]. - Since BK=16, we can unroll or loop. - `float sum0 = 0, sum1 = 0;` - `for (int k=0; k<BK; k++) { float p = p_smem[warp_id][k]; sum0 += p * v_smem[k][d0]; sum1 += p * v_smem[k][d1]; }` - But each thread does this loop independently. That's 16 iterations per thread, 2 FMAs per iteration = 32 FMAs per thread per dt. There are 16 dt and 32 kt and 64 qg. Total FMAs per thread = 32 * 16 * 32 * 64 = 1,048,576. Wait, that's half the required 2M. Why? - Let's recalculate: For PV: BQ * N * D = 8 * 512 * 1024 = 4,194,304 FMAs per query group. With 32 key tiles, each key tile contributes 8*16*1024 = 131,072 FMAs. Per thread? 256 threads. 131,072 / 256 = 512 FMAs per thread per key tile? That seems too low. Wait, total FMAs for one key tile's PV contribution is: for each query (8), each key (16), each D (1024): 8*16*1024 = 131,072 FMAs. With 256 threads, average 512 FMAs per thread per key tile. Over 32 key tiles, that's 16,384 FMAs per thread per query group. Over 64 query groups, that's 1,048,576 FMAs. This is only for the PV part. QK part is another 1,048,576 FMAs. Total 2,097,152 FMAs per thread. Yes, that matches. - In the O update loop above, each thread did 16 iterations * 2 FMAs = 32 FMAs per dt. Over 16 dt => 512 FMAs per thread per key tile. Over 32 key tiles => 16,384 FMAs per thread per query group. Over 64 query groups => 1,048,576 FMAs for PV. Perfect. So mapping gives correct FMA count. - After computing sum0, sum1, we update o_acc: - Read old o_acc: `old0 = o_smem[q][dt*DT + d0]` (or from register if we kept it). - `new0 = correction_prev * old0 + sum0;` - Write back. - Note: `correction_prev` is the same for all d for a given q. - `correction_prev` and `correction_tile` and `l_new` can be stored in shared memory arrays `m_arr[8]`, `l_arr[8]`, and maybe computed per key tile. - Since lane 0 computed m_new, l_new, it can store them. Other lanes need to read `correction_prev`. We can broadcast via smem or shuffle. Optimizing shared memory usage: - Smem layout: - float smem_q[8][64]; // 2KB (used during S stage) - float smem_k[16][64]; // 4KB (used during S stage) - float smem_v[16][64]; // 4KB (used during O stage, can reuse smem_k) - float smem_s[8][16]; // 512 bytes (scores for current key tile) - float smem_p[8][16]; // 512 bytes (weights, can reuse smem_s) - float smem_o[8][1024]; // 32KB (accumulator for O for current query group) - float smem_m[8]; // 32 bytes - float smem_l[8]; // 32 bytes - Total with reuse: - smem_q (2KB) + smem_k/v (4KB) + smem_s/p (512B) + smem_o (32KB) + smem_m/l (64B) = 38.5KB. - Wait, can we overlap smem_q with smem_v? During O stage, we don't need Q. But we might need smem_q for next key tile's S? No, we finish all key tiles for current query group, write O, then load next query group. But within a query group, we do key tile loop: S stage then O stage. After O stage, we go to next key tile. The next iteration S stage loads Q again. So we can reuse smem_v for smem_k (they are never needed simultaneously). Actually during S stage, we need smem_q and smem_k. During O stage, we need smem_p and smem_v. No overlap. So max footprint = max(2+4, 0.5+4) + 32 = 38KB. Plus small arrays. So ~38KB. That fits in 48KB easily. - Wait, do we need smem_q and smem_k simultaneously during S? Yes. So 6KB. - Do we need smem_p and smem_v simultaneously during O? Yes. But smem_p is 512B, smem_v is 4KB. So 4.5KB. - So max = 32KB (o) + 6KB (q+k) = 38KB. Good. Programming details: - We need to be careful about __syncthreads() between loading smem and using it. - Since block size is 256 and we have 8 warps, some operations like loading smem can be done by all threads. - Loading Q_smem: for each query group qg and dt, we need to load Q for 8 queries and 64 features. - Q layout: [N, D] (for this head). Q[q][d]. - Offset: base + (qg * BQ + q) * D + dt * DT + d. - We can have all 256 threads load one element each: we need 8*64=512 elements. But we only have 256 threads. So each thread loads 2 elements. - Thread tid loads: - q_idx = tid / 64? But 256/64 = 4, not 8. Let's do: - For loading Q_smem, we can use a simple 1D loop: - for (int i = tid; i < BQ * DT; i += blockDim.x) { int q = i / DT; int d = i % DT; smem_q[q][d] = Q[...]; } - This is efficient coalescing? Threads access consecutive elements if i is consecutive. Since Q is row-major [N][D], consecutive i means consecutive d, same q until wrap. This is coalesced within each query. - Similarly for K_smem: for (int i = tid; i < BK * DT; i += blockDim.x), load K[kt*BK + k][dt*DT + d]. - For V_smem. - For O output: after all key tiles, write smem_o to global memory O for the query group. Wait, there is an issue. The query group qg iterates 64 times. The O accumulator for the query group is stored in smem_o (32KB). After finishing all key tiles for the query group, we must write O to global memory. Then reset smem_m, smem_l, smem_o for the next query group. This is straightforward. Let's carefully write out the kernel steps: ``` extern "C" __global__ void fused_attention_kernel( const float* __restrict__ Q, const float* __restrict__ K, const float* __restrict__ V, float* __restrict__ O, int B, int H, int N, int D, float scale) { // Block indices int b = blockIdx.x; int h = blockIdx.y; int tid = threadIdx.x; int warp_id = tid / 32; int lane_id = tid % 32; // Base offset for this head int head_offset = ((b * H + h) * N) * D; // Smem declarations __shared__ float smem_q[8][64]; // BQ x DT __shared__ float smem_k[16][64]; // BK x DT // Reuse smem_k for V later __shared__ float smem_s[8][16]; // scores const int BQ = 8; const int BK = 16; const int DT = 64; __shared__ float smem_o[8][1024]; // BQ x D __shared__ float smem_m[8]; __shared__ float smem_l[8]; // Each block processes one head for (int qg = 0; qg < N / BQ; qg++) { // Initialize smem_o, smem_m, smem_l for (int i = tid; i < BQ * D; i += blockDim.x) { smem_o[i / D][i % D] = 0.0f; } if (tid < BQ) { smem_m[tid] = -INFINITY; smem_l[tid] = 0.0f; } __syncthreads(); // Load Q for this query group? We will load per dt in key tile loop. // Actually we can load all Q for this group once? 8*1024=8192 floats. // 8192 * 4 = 32KB. We have smem_o (32KB) being used, so we can't load all Q at once. // So we load Q per D tile as planned. for (int kt = 0; kt < N / BK; kt++) { // Compute scores S for this key tile // Initialize smem_s // Actually we compute into registers first, accumulate, then write to smem_s at end. float local_acc = 0.0f; int q_local = warp_id; int k_local = lane_id % BK; // 0..15 int part = lane_id / BK; // 0 or 1, each handles 32 elements of DT for (int dt = 0; dt < D / DT; dt++) { // Load Q for (int i = tid; i < BQ * DT; i += blockDim.x) { int q = i / DT; int d = i % DT; int q_idx = qg * BQ + q; smem_q[q][d] = Q[head_offset + q_idx * D + dt * DT + d]; } // Load K for (int i = tid; i < BK * DT; i += blockDim.x) { int k = i / DT; int d = i % DT; int k_idx = kt * BK + k; smem_k[k][d] = K[head_offset + k_idx * D + dt * DT + d]; } __syncthreads(); // Compute partial dot product // q_local = warp_id, k_local = lane_id % BK // We access smem_q[q_local][d] and smem_k[k_local][d] // Each thread handles d from part*(DT/2) to part*(DT/2) + DT/2 - 1 int d_start = part * (DT / 2); #pragma unroll for (int d = 0; d < DT / 2; d++) { int d_offset = d_start + d; local_acc += smem_q[q_local][d_offset] * smem_k[k_local][d_offset]; } __syncthreads(); // before next load } // Reduce local_acc between the two threads of the same key // lane_id and lane_id^16 correspond to same key, different parts float other = __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_acc, 16); // For lane_id 0..15, we want sum; for 16..31, also sum if we want. // Actually __shfl_xor_sync exchanges with lane_id ^ 16. // So both lanes get the other part. float s_val = local_acc + other; // Only store from lanes 0..15 to avoid duplication if (lane_id < BK) { smem_s[warp_id][lane_id] = s_val * scale; } __syncthreads(); // Now do softmax for this key tile // Read s_val for this lane's key (only lanes 0..15 valid) float my_s = (lane_id < BK) ? smem_s[warp_id][lane_id] : -INFINITY; // Warp reduce max over 32 lanes float m_val = my_s; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { float other_m = __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, m_val, offset); m_val = fmaxf(m_val, other_m); } // m_val now has max over all lanes. But shuffle_down duplicates; need careful. // Wait, __shfl_down_sync copies from lane + offset. For offset=16, lane 0 gets from lane 16. // Lane 0 and lane 16 both have my_s (for key 0 and 16? Actually lane 16 has key 0). // So lane 0 gets key0_part1's s_val. lane 0 fmaxs with its own key0_part0 s_val. Good. // But lane 1 and lane 17 both have key1. etc. // After offset=16, lanes 0..15 have max of their key and key+16? No, lane 0..15 have max(key_k, key_{k+16})? But key_{k+16} corresponds to lane 16+k which also has key k. So it's just max of the two copies, which are identical after shfl_xor sum? Wait, __shfl_xor gave the same s_val to both lanes (since local_acc+other is same). So m_val after offset=16 is just that same value. // Then offset=8: lane 0 gets from lane 8 (key 8). Lane 0 has key0. We want max over all keys 0..15. This works! Because lanes 0..15 represent keys 0..15. // But wait, lane 16 gets from lane 24 (key 8's duplicate). The values in lanes 16..31 are the same as 0..15. The reduction across all 32 lanes will compute max of all keys because values in 16..31 are duplicates of 0..15. So it's fine; we just need lane 0's result. // Actually `__shfl_down_sync` for offset>=16 for lane 16..31 will read out of range (wrap around or same lane). According to CUDA docs, if src lane is out of range, it returns the value from the source lane modulo warp size? Actually for `__shfl_down_sync`, if `srcLane >= 32`, the operation returns the value from the same lane (i.e., `var`). So for lane 16, offset=16 => src=32 >=32 => returns `var`. So lane 16..31 will effectively ignore higher offsets. That's fine because we only care about lane 0's result. // Let's just do the standard warp reduce using `__shfl_xor_sync` which is simpler for max. m_val = my_s; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { float other_m = __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, m_val, offset); m_val = fmaxf(m_val, other_m); } // After this, all lanes have the same m_val (max over warp). Good. // Now compute l_tile = sum exp(my_s - m_val) float exp_val = (lane_id < BK) ? expf(my_s - m_val) : 0.0f; float l_val = exp_val; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { l_val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, l_val, offset); } // l_val is sum over warp (all lanes), same in all lanes. // Update global softmax stats for this query float m_prev, l_prev; if (lane_id == 0) { m_prev = smem_m[warp_id]; l_prev = smem_l[warp_id]; } m_prev = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, m_prev, 0); l_prev = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, l_prev, 0); float m_new = fmaxf(m_prev, m_val); float corr_prev = expf(m_prev - m_new); float corr_tile = expf(m_val - m_new); float l_new = corr_prev * l_prev + corr_tile * l_val; // Compute p weights for each key: p = exp(my_s - m_new) = exp_val * corr_tile // Wait: exp(my_s - m_new) = exp(my_s - m_val) * exp(m_val - m_new) = exp_val * corr_tile. float p_weight = exp_val * corr_tile; // Store p_weight to smem_s or a dedicated smem_p // We can reuse smem_s for p weights since we don't need scores anymore. if (lane_id < BK) { smem_s[warp_id][lane_id] = p_weight; } // Store updated m and l if (lane_id == 0) { smem_m[warp_id] = m_new; smem_l[warp_id] = l_new; } __syncthreads(); // Now update O accumulator using p_weights and V tile for (int dt = 0; dt < D / DT; dt++) { // Load V tile for (int i = tid; i < BK * DT; i += blockDim.x) { int k = i / DT; int d = i % DT; int k_idx = kt * BK + k; smem_k[k][d] = V[head_offset + k_idx * D + dt * DT + d]; // Reuse smem_k buffer for V (since we are in O stage) } __syncthreads(); // Each warp handles one query q_local = warp_id // Each thread handles two d's: d0 = lane_id, d1 = lane_id + 32 int d0 = lane_id; int d1 = lane_id + 32; float sum0 = 0.0f; float sum1 = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int k = 0; k < BK; k++) { float p = smem_s[q_local][k]; sum0 += p * smem_k[k][d0]; sum1 += p * smem_k[k][d1]; } // Apply correction_prev to old o and add sum // o_acc is in smem_o[q_local][dt*DT + d] int d_base = dt * DT; float old0, old1; // We need to read old o. Each thread reads its own two positions. // But there is no atomic needed; they are distinct addresses. old0 = smem_o[q_local][d_base + d0]; old1 = smem_o[q_local][d_base + d1]; float new0 = corr_prev * old0 + sum0; float new1 = corr_prev * old1 + sum1; smem_o[q_local][d_base + d0] = new0; smem_o[q_local][d_base + d1] = new1; __syncthreads(); } } // end key tiles // After all key tiles, normalize O by l for (int i = tid; i < BQ * D; i += blockDim.x) { int q = i / D; int d = i % D; float l_val = smem_l[q]; float o_val = smem_o[q][d]; int q_idx = qg * BQ + q; O[head_offset + q_idx * D + d] = o_val / l_val; } __syncthreads(); } // end query groups } ``` Wait, there is a subtle bug in the max reduction. `my_s` is only valid for lanes 0..15; lanes 16..31 are set to -INFINITY (or 0 for exp but for max, -INFINITY). But the warp reduction `__shfl_xor_sync` will compare. Since lanes 16..31 have -INFINITY, they won't affect the max if lanes 0..15 have real values. So `m_val` computed by all lanes will be correct. However, there is a problem: `__shfl_xor_sync` with offset 16 will exchange lane 0 and lane 16. Lane 0 has `my_s` for key 0. Lane 16 has `my_s` but we set it to -INFINITY. So after the first XOR, lane 0's m_val becomes max(key0, -INF) = key0. But lane 16's m_val becomes max(-INF, key0) = key0. Actually both get key0. That means lanes 0..15 and 16..31 will have the values of the corresponding lanes they exchange with. After all offsets, all lanes will have the max of all keys where at least one lane had that value. Since lanes 0..15 have the actual values, and lanes 16..31 have -INF, the max across all 32 will be the max of keys 0..15. So m_val in all lanes will be correct. Good. But wait, `exp_val` for lanes 16..31 is 0. So l_val includes 0 for those lanes. Warp reduction sum will only sum the 16 valid lanes. That's correct. Now, a performance concern: the `__syncthreads()` inside the `dt` loop for V loading and update. Since we have 16 dt iterations per key tile and 32 key tiles = 512 __syncthreads() calls inside the inner loop (plus the ones in S stage). That's about 1024 __syncthreads per query group. Per block, 64 query groups => ~65k __syncthreads. This is a lot of synchronization overhead. However, `__syncthreads()` within a block on modern GPUs is relatively fast, but it might still add up. We can try to reduce syncs by having threads load V into smem without full sync? No, we need all threads to see the loaded V before using it. But what if we load V for the next dt while processing current dt? That's double buffering. We can allocate two buffers for V in smem and use them alternately. But the sync is still needed before consumption. However, we can maybe remove the `__syncthreads()` after writing O, because threads within a warp access distinct d indices, but they all read V_smem which was loaded and synced. We need to ensure that no thread proceeds to load the next V tile before all threads have finished reading the current one. Since the loop iteration is the same for all threads (they all do `for dt...`), and `__syncthreads()` after loading V is needed. But do we need a `__syncthreads()` after writing O? The next iteration loads V into the same smem_k. Some threads might be writing O (to smem_o) while others have moved to load V. But O writes go to smem_o, and V loads go to smem_k. These are disjoint smem arrays, so no conflict. However, we need a `__syncthreads()` at the end of the `dt` loop to ensure all writes to smem_o are done before any thread moves to the next key tile? No, the next key tile reads V and writes smem_k, and also reads smem_o. But all threads are in lockstep within the `dt` loop. After the last `dt`, we exit the dt loop and go to next `kt`. We have a `__syncthreads()` at the start of the next dt loop's V load. But between the last dt and the next key tile, we hit the top of the outer `kt` loop. There is no `__syncthreads()` after the last dt of the previous kt before the first dt of the next kt, except if we put one before `for dt=0`. Actually after the inner dt loop, we go to next `kt`. The first thing in the next `kt` is computing scores S, which needs `__syncthreads()` after loading Q and K. But we also need to make sure all threads have finished reading smem_k from the previous iteration before some thread starts loading Q/K into smem_k in the next S stage? No, in the S stage we load into smem_k. During O stage we use smem_k for V. In the next S stage, we overwrite smem_k with K. This is fine because the previous iteration is fully complete for all threads. There is an implicit sync because all threads execute the `kt` loop in lockstep. So just placing `__syncthreads()` after loading Q/K in S stage and after loading V in O stage should be sufficient. But actually in the `dt` loop of O stage: - load V - __syncthreads() - compute and write O // loop back, load next V. No need for __syncthreads after write O because next iteration loads V into smem_k, which is different from smem_o. Some warps might be ahead loading V while others are still writing O. But O writes are to smem_o; V loads are to smem_k. These don't alias. So it's safe! Thus we can remove the __syncthreads after O computation inside the dt loop. - However, we must be careful: inside the dt loop, after `__syncthreads()` following V load, all threads read smem_k. Then they write smem_o. Since smem_o is not read by any other thread in this iteration, no sync needed. Next iteration: we load V into smem_k. Threads that finished writing O can start loading next V into smem_k. But threads that are still writing O might be slower. If they catch up, they might start reading smem_k before it's fully loaded by the faster threads. So we need a `__syncthreads()` after V load at the start of each iteration. That's enough. - Wait, but the load into smem_k is done cooperatively by all threads. Faster threads might finish loading and then slower threads might still be loading. `__syncthreads()` after the load loop ensures all loads are visible. Good. - Similarly, in the S stage dt loop, we load Q and K, then __syncthreads(), then compute, then __syncthreads() before the next iteration's load. Actually after compute, we might not need __syncthreads if the next dt iteration loads into different smem? No, it loads into smem_q and smem_k again. Some threads might still be reading smem_q/k from previous dt while others are writing to them for next dt. So we need __syncthreads() at the end of dt loop iteration (after compute, before next load). However, Q and K loads in the next iteration will overwrite. But if some threads from the previous iteration are still reading smem_q (from the compute stage), they could be reading new data. So we need a __syncthreads() after compute. Since the compute stage is fully within registers (reading smem_q and smem_k into registers), and all threads in the block participate, after the compute loop we need __syncthreads() before the next load. Unless some threads are faster and start loading while slower threads still read. So yes, __syncthreads() is needed. Number of __syncthreads per dt for S stage: 2 (one after load, one after compute). For O stage: 1 (after load V). Actually for O stage, after O write, next iteration loads V. We need __syncthreads after O write. Let's keep it simple and safe: place __syncthreads after compute in S dt loop, and after write in O dt loop. Total per dt: 3. Total per key tile: (16*2 + 16*2) = 64? No: S dt loop (16 iterations): load Q+K, sync, compute, sync. -> 32 syncs. O dt loop (16 iterations): load V, sync, compute+write O, sync. -> 32 syncs. Total per key tile: 64 syncs. Over 32 key tiles: 2048 syncs per qg. Over 64 qg: 131k syncs per block. That seems like a lot but maybe okay? Each __syncthreads is a barrier instruction. On H100, it's cheap but not free. 131k * 1024 blocks = 134M syncs. That might be a bottleneck. Wait, we can avoid per-dt syncs in O stage by loading V for all D tiles at once? No, D=1024, V tile for all D would be 16*1024*4 = 64KB. That exceeds 48KB. But we can request more shared memory. H100 allows up to 227KB. callcompile_kernel { "kernel_code": "import torch\nimport torch.nn as nn\nfrom torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline\n\ncuda_source = '''\n#include <torch/extension.h>\n#include <cuda_runtime.h>\n#include <math.h>\n\n#ifndef M_PI\n#define M_PI 3.14159265358979323846\n#endif\n\n#define BQ 8\n#define BK 16\n#define DT 64\n#define PAD 4\n\n__global__ void fused_attention_kernel(\n const float* __restrict__ Q,\n const float* __restrict__ K,\n const float* __restrict__ V,\n float* __restrict__ O,\n int B, int H, int N, int D,\n float scale)\n{\n int b = blockIdx.x;\n int h = blockIdx.y;\n int tid = threadIdx.x;\n int warp_id = tid / 32;\n int lane_id = tid % 32;\n\n int head_offset = ((b * H + h) * N) * D;\n\n __shared__ float smem_q[BQ][DT + PAD];\n __shared__ float smem_kv[BK][DT + PAD];\n __shared__ float smem_p[BQ][BK];\n __shared__ float smem_m[BQ];\n __shared__ float smem_l[BQ];\n __shared__ float smem_o[BQ][1024 + PAD];\n\n for (int qg = 0; qg < N; qg += BQ) {\n // init O, m, l\n for (int i = tid; i < BQ * D; i += blockDim.x) {\n int q = i / D;\n int d = i % D;\n smem_o[q][d] = 0.0f;\n }\n if (tid < BQ) {\n smem_m[tid] = -1e20f;\n smem_l[tid] = 0.0f;\n }\n __syncthreads();\n\n for (int kt = 0; kt < N; kt += BK) {\n float local_acc = 0.0f;\n int q_local = warp_id;\n int k_local = lane_id % BK;\n int part = lane_id / BK; // 0 or 1\n\n // compute scores for this key tile\n for (int dt = 0; dt < D; dt += DT) {\n // load Q\n for (int i = tid; i < BQ * DT; i += blockDim.x) {\n int q = i / DT;\n int d = i % DT;\n int q_idx = qg + q;\n smem_q[q][d] = Q[head_offset + q_idx * D + dt + d];\n }\n // load K\n for (int i = tid; i < BK * DT; i += blockDim.x) {\n int k = i / DT;\n int d = i % DT;\n int k_idx = kt + k;\n smem_kv[k][d] = K[head_offset + k_idx * D + dt + d];\n }\n __syncthreads();\n\n int d_start = part * (DT / 2);\n #pragma unroll\n for (int d = 0; d < DT / 2; ++d) {\n int d_offset = d_start + d;\n local_acc += smem_q[q_local][d_offset] * smem_kv[k_local][d_offset];\n }\n __syncthreads();\n }\n\n // reduce across the two parts\n float other = __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_acc, 16);\n float s_val = local_acc + other;\n s_val *= scale;\n\n if (lane_id < BK) {\n smem_p[warp_id][lane_id] = s_val;\n }\n __syncthreads();\n\n // online softmax for this key tile\n float my_s = (lane_id < BK) ? smem_p[warp_id][lane_id] : -1e20f;\n\n // warp max\n float m_val = my_s;\n #pragma unroll\n for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) {\n float other_m = __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, m_val, offset);\n m_val = fmaxf(m_val, other_m);\n }\n\n // warp sum of exp\n float exp_val = (lane_id < BK) ? expf(my_s - m_val) : 0.0f;\n float l_val = exp_val;\n #pragma unroll\n for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) {\n l_val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, l_val, offset);\n }\n\n // update running stats\n float m_prev, l_prev;\n if (lane_id == 0) {\n m_prev = smem_m[warp_id];\n l_prev = smem_l[warp_id];\n }\n m_prev = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, m_prev, 0);\n l_prev = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, l_prev, 0);\n\n float m_new = fmaxf(m_prev, m_val);\n float corr_prev = expf(m_prev - m_new);\n float corr_tile = expf(m_val - m_new);\n float l_new = corr_prev * l_prev + corr_tile * l_val;\n\n if (lane_id == 0) {\n smem_m[warp_id] = m_new;\n smem_l[warp_id] = l_new;\n }\n\n // store p weights\n float p_weight = exp_val * corr_tile;\n if (lane_id < BK) {\n smem_p[warp_id][lane_id] = p_weight;\n }\n __syncthreads();\n\n // update O accumulator\n for (int dt = 0; dt < D; dt += DT) {\n // load V tile into smem_kv\n for (int i = tid; i < BK * DT; i += blockDim.x) {\n int k = i / DT;\n int d = i % DT;\n int k_idx = kt + k;\n smem_kv[k][d] = V[head_offset + k_idx * D + dt + d];\n }\n __syncthreads();\n\n int d0 = lane_id;\n int d1 = lane_id + 32;\n int d_base = dt;\n\n float sum0 = 0.0f;\n float sum1 = 0.0f;\n #pragma unroll\n for (int k = 0; k < BK; ++k) {\n float p = smem_p[q_local][k];\n sum0 += p * smem_kv[k][d0];\n sum1 += p * smem_kv[k][d1];\n }\n\n float old0 = smem_o[q_local][d_base + d0];\n float old1 = smem_o[q_local][d_base + d1];\n smem_o[q_local][d_base + d0] = corr_prev * old0 + sum0;\n smem_o[q_local][d_base + d1] = corr_prev * old1 + sum1;\n\n __syncthreads();\n }\n }\n\n // write out\n for (int i = tid; i < BQ * D; i += blockDim.x) {\n int q = i / D;\n int d = i % D;\n float l_val = smem_l[q];\n float o_val = smem_o[q][d];\n int q_idx = qg + q;\n O[head_offset + q_idx * D + d] = o_val / l_val;\n }\n __syncthreads();\n }\n}\n\ntorch::Tensor forward(torch::Tensor Q, torch::Tensor K, torch::Tensor V) {\n auto O = torch::empty_like(Q);\n int B = Q.size(0);\n int H = Q.size(1);\n int N = Q.size(2);\n int D = Q.size(3);\n float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)D);\n dim3 grid(B, H);\n dim3 block(256);\n fused_attention_kernel<<<grid, block>>>(\n Q.data_ptr<float>(), K.data_ptr<float>(), V.data_ptr<float>(), O.data_ptr<float>(),\n B, H, N, D, scale);\n return O;\n}\n'''\n\nload_inline(\n name=\"fused_attention\",\n cpp_sources=\"torch::Tensor forward(torch::Tensor Q, torch::Tensor K, torch::Tensor V);\",\n cuda_sources=cuda_source,\n functions=[\"forward\"],\n extra_cuda_cflags=[\"-O3\", \"--use_fast_math\"],\n verbose=False,\n)\n\nclass ModelNew(nn.Module):\n def __init__(self):\n super(ModelNew, self).__init__()\n\n def forward(self, Q: torch.Tensor, K: torch.Tensor, V: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:\n Q = Q.contiguous()\n K = K.contiguous()\n V = V.contiguous()\n return fused_attention.forward(Q, K, V)\n\n# dummy check that module loads\nif __name__ == \"__main__\":\n pass\n" }

dt += DT) {\n // load Q\n for (int i = tid; i < BQ * DT; i += blockDim.x) {\n int q = i / DT;\n int d = i % DT;\n int q_idx = qg + q;\n smem_q[q][d] = Q[head_offset + q_idx * D + dt + d];\n }\n // load K\n for (int i = tid; i < BK * DT; i += blockDim.x) {\n int k = i / DT;\n int d = i % DT;\n int k_idx = kt + k;\n smem_kv[k][d] = K[head_offset + k_idx * D + dt + d];\n }\n __syncthreads();\n\n int d_start = part * (DT / 2);\n #pragma unroll\n for (int d = 0; d < DT / 2; ++d) {\n int d_offset = d_start + d;\n local_acc += smem_q[q_local][d_offset] * smem_kv[k_local][d_offset];\n }\n __syncthreads();\n }\n\n // reduce across the two parts\n float other = __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, local_acc, 16);\n float s_val = local_acc + other;\n s_val *= scale;\n\n if (lane_id < BK) {\n smem_p[warp_id][lane_id] = s_val;\n }\n __syncthreads();\n\n // online softmax for this key tile\n float my_s = (lane_id < BK) ? smem_p[warp_id][lane_id] : -1e20f;\n\n // warp max\n float m_val = my_s;\n #pragma unroll\n for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) {\n float other_m = __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, m_val, offset);\n m_val = fmaxf(m_val, other_m);\n }\n\n // warp sum of exp\n float exp_val = (lane_id < BK) ? expf(my_s - m_val) : 0.0f;\n float l_val = exp_val;\n #pragma unroll\n for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) {\n l_val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, l_val, offset);\n }\n\n // update running stats\n float m_prev, l_prev;\n if (lane_id == 0) {\n m_prev = smem_m[warp_id];\n l_prev = smem_l[warp_id];\n }\n m_prev = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, m_prev, 0);\n l_prev = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, l_prev, 0);\n\n float m_new = fmaxf(m_prev, m_val);\n float corr_prev = expf(m_prev - m_new);\n float corr_tile = expf(m_val - m_new);\n float l_new = corr_prev * l_prev + corr_tile * l_val;\n\n if (lane_id == 0) {\n smem_m[warp_id] = m_new;\n smem_l[warp_id] = l_new;\n }\n\n // store p weights\n float p_weight = exp_val * corr_tile;\n if (lane_id < BK) {\n smem_p[warp_id][lane_id] = p_weight;\n }\n __syncthreads();\n\n // update O accumulator\n for (int dt = 0; dt < D; dt += DT) {\n // load V tile into smem_kv\n for (int i = tid; i < BK * DT; i += blockDim.x) {\n int k = i / DT;\n int d = i % DT;\n int k_idx = kt + k;\n smem_kv[k][d] = V[head_offset + k_idx * D + dt + d];\n }\n __syncthreads();\n\n int d0 = lane_id;\n int d1 = lane_id + 32;\n int d_base = dt;\n\n float sum0 = 0.0f;\n float sum1 = 0.0f;\n #pragma unroll\n for (int k = 0; k < BK; ++k) {\n float p = smem_p[q_local][k];\n sum0 += p * smem_kv[k][d0];\n sum1 += p * smem_kv[k][d1];\n }\n\n float old0 = smem_o[q_local][d_base + d0];\n float old1 = smem_o[q_local][d_base + d1];\n smem_o[q_local][d_base + d0] = corr_prev * old0 + sum0;\n smem_o[q_local][d_base + d1] = corr_prev * old1 + sum1;\n\n __syncthreads();\n }\n }\n\n // write out\n for (int i = tid; i < BQ * D; i += blockDim.x) {\n int q = i / D;\n int d = i % D;\n float l_val = smem_l[q];\n float o_val = smem_o[q][d];\n int q_idx = qg + q;\n O[head_offset + q_idx * D + d] = o_val / l_val;\n }\n __syncthreads();\n }\n}\n\ntorch::Tensor forward(torch::Tensor Q, torch::Tensor K, torch::Tensor V) {\n auto O = torch::empty_like(Q);\n int B = Q.size(0);\n int H = Q.size(1);\n int N = Q.size(2);\n int D = Q.size(3);\n float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)D);\n dim3 grid(B, H);\n dim3 block(256);\n fused_attention_kernel<<<grid, block>>>(\n Q.data_ptr<float>(), K.data_ptr<float>(), V.data_ptr<float>(), O.data_ptr<float>(),\n B, H, N, D, scale);\n return O;\n}\n'''\n\nfused_attention = load_inline(\n name=\"fused_attention\",\n cpp_sources=\"torch::Tensor forward(torch::Tensor Q, torch::Tensor K, torch::Tensor V);\",\n cuda_sources=cuda_source,\n functions=[\"forward\"],\n extra_cuda_cflags=[\"-O3\", \"--use_fast_math\"],\n verbose=False,\n)\n\nclass ModelNew(nn.Module):\n def __init__(self):\n super(ModelNew, self).__init__()\n\n def forward(self, Q: torch.Tensor, K: torch.Tensor, V: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:\n Q = Q.contiguous()\n K = K.contiguous()\n V = V.contiguous()\n return fused_attention.forward(Q, K, V)\n\n# dummy check that module loads\nif __name__ == \"__main__\":\n pass\n" }

Let me think about how to structure the kernel: ```cpp __global__ void attention_kernel( const float* Q, const float* K, const float* V, float* O, int B, int H, int N, int D ) { int tid = threadIdx.x; int q_per_block = 256; // blockDim.x int q_block_id = blockIdx.z; // 0 or 1 for N=512 int q = q_block_id * q_per_block + tid; int b = blockIdx.x; int h = blockIdx.y; if (q >= N) return; // read Q[q][0:D] into registers in chunks // iterate over all keys // use shared memory for K and V tiles int head_offset = ((b * H + h) * N + q) * D; int head_offset_kv = ((b * H + h) * N) * D; float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)D); float m = -1e20f; float l = 0.0f; // O accumulator: process in chunks // We can't keep 1024 floats in registers per thread. // We'll process D in chunks of, say, 64. for (int d_base = 0; d_base < D; d_base += DT) { float o_acc = 0.0f; // Wait, we need to interleave keys and D chunks simultaneously. // Standard approach: inner loop over keys, but that means we need Q for each key. // Better: outer loop over keys, inner loop over D chunks. // Load Q[q][d_base:d_base+DT] once, then iterate over key tiles. // But for online softmax, we need scores for ALL keys before updating O? // No, we can do online softmax at the key level. // Actually, if we process D in chunks, we need partial scores per key tile. // This gets complicated. // Alternative: keep all O partials in a small shared memory per thread, // but 256 threads * 1024 floats = 1MB, which is too much. } } ``` The problem is that for online softmax, the correction factor for O accumulators depends on the global max, which isn't known until all keys of a tile are processed. To make score storage coalesced, we need thread t to access element t, t+blockDim, t+2*blockDim, etc. So we need to store scores as transposed[score_idx][thread] instead of [thread][score_idx]. But these scores are in local memory, and the compiler decides the layout. The layout for local arrays is typically row-major with the thread index as the slowest varying dimension, which means consecutive elements in the array are consecutive in memory. Wait, for `float scores[512];` in a thread, the compiler allocates `512 * 4 = 2048` bytes per thread. Memory layout is thread 0: bytes 0-2047, thread 1: bytes 2048-4095, etc. (Actually it's often interleaved in groups of 128B for coalescing, but for spilled arrays I'm not sure.) If the layout is thread-interleaved, accessing `scores[i]` by all threads in a warp would be perfectly coalesced! Wait, how does the compiler store local arrays? I recall NVIDIA docs say that access to local memory is only ever fully coalesced when ALL threads in a warp access the same address. Otherwise, it's strided. Actually, for 1D arrays, the compiler tries to ensure that `array[i]` by thread `t` is coalesced with `array[i]` by thread `t+1`. This means the elements `scores[i]` for all threads in a warp are stored together. Actually, the standard compiler behavior for `float local[512]` is to allocate them such that `local[i]` for all threads in a warp are contiguous. More precisely, the layout is: for each `i`, `thread0_local[i], thread1_local[i], ..., thread31_local[i], padding to 128B boundary`. This makes per-warp access to `local[i]` coalesced! But a warp of threads all accessing `local[i]` at the same time would be coalesced. In our algorithm: Pass 1: - Thread t computes score for key k over all D, writes to local[k]. - At key k, all threads in a warp write to their local[k]. This IS coalesced! Pass 2: - Thread t reads local[k] for key k. - All threads in a warp read from their own local[k] at the same time, which is also coalesced. WAIT, but pass 2 also needs ALL scores for a thread to compute softmax. The softmax reads scores sequentially: ```cpp for (int k=0; k<N; k++) s[k] = scores[k]; ``` With `float scores[512]`, and all threads reading `scores[0]`, then `scores[1]`, etc., at each k all threads read their local[k]. This is coalesced. Then we need to find max over 512 scores per thread. This is done in registers, no memory issue. Then compute exp(scores[k] - max) and sum. Again, read scores[k] sequentially, coalesced. Then accumulate V: read scores[k] again for weights. Wait, do we need to store scores at all? If we do two passes: - Pass 1: compute all scores, track max. - We only need max from pass 1. We don't need to store scores! - Pass 2: recompute scores and accumulate V with softmax weights. This avoids storing scores entirely! But it recomputes the dot products: - Pass 1: Q·K for all 512 keys = 512*1024 = 524k FMAs. - Pass 2: Q·K again for all 512 keys = 524k FMAs. - Plus V accumulation: 512*1024 = 524k FMAs. Total: ~1.57M FMAs per query. Compute total: 524288 queries * 1.57M = 823B FMAs. At 67 TFLOPS = 12.3ms. But if we're compute bound at 12ms, that's the time. But PyTorch reference might do something slower, especially if it's not using flash attention. However, this approach reads Q and K twice each. Can we do better? Alternative: keep scores in registers or shared memory to avoid recomputation. With 512 threads per block processing 512 queries in one head: - We could have shared memory store a tile of K and a tile of scores. - Actually, instead of each thread storing its own 512 scores, we could process keys in tiles. - For each key tile of 16 keys: - All 512 threads compute their scores for these 16 keys. - For 512 threads, 16 keys each, that's 8192 scores. - Store in shared memory? 8192 * 4 = 32KB. That's very reasonable! - Run softmax on the 16 scores + running stats - Accumulate V for these 16 keys - Discard scores Wait, this is EXACTLY the online softmax tile approach, but with the twist that each thread handles one query and all keys in the tile, and scores for a tile are stored in shared memory or registers. Actually, with 16 keys per tile: - Each thread computes 16 scores (one per key in tile). - It can keep them in 16 registers! - Then do warp-level or thread-level softmax over 16 elements. - With online softmax, we update running stats and O accumulator. - No need to store scores in shared memory at all! This is the key insight. Let me formalize: Per thread (handles 1 query): ```cpp float m = -1e20f; // running max float l = 0.0f; // running sum exp float o[DT]; // partial output accumulator, for D processed in chunks of DT for (int kt = 0; kt < N; kt += BK) { // BK = 16 // compute BK scores for this query float s[BK]; // 16 registers #pragma unroll for (int k = 0; k < BK; ++k) { s[k] = 0; } for (int d = 0; d < D; ++d) { float q_val = Q[q*D + d]; // each thread loads its own Q once per D #pragma unroll for (int k = 0; k < BK; ++k) { float k_val = K[(kt+k)*D + d]; // broadcast or coalesced load from shared s[k] += q_val * k_val; } } // apply scale #pragma unroll for (int k = 0; k < BK; ++k) s[k] *= scale; // online softmax for this tile float tile_max = s[0]; #pragma unroll for (int k = 1; k < BK; ++k) tile_max = fmaxf(tile_max, s[k]); float new_m = fmaxf(m, tile_max); float corr_m = expf(m - new_m); float corr_tile = expf(tile_max - new_m); float tile_sum = 0; #pragma unroll for (int k = 0; k < BK; ++k) tile_sum += expf(s[k] - tile_max); // update O accumulator for each d_chunk: load O accumulators for k in 0..BK-1: p = expf(s[k] - new_m); V_val = V[(kt+k)*D + d]; o[d_chunk] = o[d_chunk] * corr_m + p * V_val; // wait, this isn't right. ``` Actually, the standard online softmax update for O is: ```cpp O_new = O_old * exp(m_old - m_new) + sum(exp(s_i - m_new) * V_i) ``` So for each key: ```cpp float p = expf(s[k] - new_m); #pragma unroll for (int d = 0; d < DT; ++d) { O[d] = O[d] * corr_m + p * V[(kt+k)*D + d]; } l = l * corr_m + tile_sum * corr_tile; ``` But wait, `corr_m` is applied to all elements of O. This is correct. And `p = expf(s[k] - new_m)` is the weight for each key. The issue is: we need to iterate over keys first, then D, or D first then keys? Standard approach: iterate over D chunks, and for each D chunk, iterate over keys to accumulate. But with 16 keys and DT=64, the inner loop would be: ```cpp for each D chunk: for each key k: p = expf(s[k] - new_m); for d in chunk: o[d] = o[d] * corr_m + p * V_val; ``` Wait, `corr_m` should be applied ONCE to all of O, not per key. So: ```cpp for each D chunk: #pragma unroll for (int d = 0; d < DT; ++d) o[d] *= corr_m; for each key k: p = expf(s[k] - new_m); #pragma unroll for (int d = 0; d < DT; ++d) o[d] += p * V[(kt+k)*D + base + d]; ``` This reduces the number of multiplications by factor BK. But we need `corr_m` per tile. Wait, is this correct? Online softmax update: At tile t, we have old accumulator `O_old` with old max `m_old`. We compute tile max `m_t` and new max `m_new = max(m_old, m_t)`. The full output should be: `O_new = O_old * exp(m_old - m_new) / Z_new * Z_old + sum_i exp(s_i - m_new) * V_i / Z_new` But in the standard flash attention formulation, the running O accumulator stores `O = sum(exp(s_i - m_running) * V_i)`, and we don't divide by L until the end. So when we update: ```cpp O_new = O_old * exp(m_old - m_new) + sum_i exp(s_i - m_new) * V_i L_new = L_old * exp(m_old - m_new) + sum_i exp(s_i - m_new) ``` Then at end, `O_final = O_new / L_new`. So yes, `corr_m = exp(m_old - m_new)` should be applied to the old accumulator once. Then add contributions from the new tile. But there's a subtlety: if the old accumulator O_old corresponds to previous keys, and then we add new key contributions, each with their own `exp(s_i - m_new) * V_i`, that's correct. So the algorithm per D chunk: ```cpp for (int d = 0; d < DT; ++d) o_local[d] *= corr_m; for (int k = 0; k < BK; ++k) { float p = expf(s[k] - new_m); for (int d = 0; d < DT; ++d) { o_local[d] += p * smem_v[k][d]; } } ``` With BK=16, we do 16 loads of V and 16 * DT FMAs. If DT=32, that's 512 FMAs. Plus the initial multiply by corr_m (32 FMAs). And the 16 exp() computations. This fits in shared memory! - Similarly V tile = 64KB. - Total shared memory = 128KB + a bit for smem_q etc. Under 227KB. Wait, each thread needs to load Q values. Each thread processes one query. Q for that query can be loaded directly from global memory. Actually, Q is only read once per query, and each thread handles one query, so Q can be in global memory. Actually, L1 cache on Ampere/Hopper can serve multiple requests per cycle but not necessarily broadcast to 512 threads. Wait, shared memory banks: 32 banks, each 32 bits wide. To broadcast, multiple threads access the same 32-bit address. A broadcast occurs when all threads in a warp read the same address - this is handled with no bank conflicts. But if 16 warps all try to read the same shared memory address simultaneously, they can't all be served in one cycle because shared memory only has 32 banks/ports. It would take multiple cycles, but still much faster than multiple L1/L2 accesses. So yes, shared memory is good for data that's read by many threads. But shared memory limits occupancy. Let me think about the memory pattern. If we don't use shared memory for K/V, and each thread does: ```cpp for each key k: float score = 0; for each d: score += Q[q*D + d] * K[k*D + d]; ``` Then all 512 threads (for 512 queries) are executing: ``` tid 0: load Q[0*D+d], K[k*D+d] tid 1: load Q[1*D+d], K[k*D+d] ... tid 511: load Q[511*D+d], K[k*D+d] ``` For a given d and k, all 512 threads load the SAME K[k*D+d] address, but different Q addresses. The Q loads are perfectly coalesced (thread t loads Q[t*D+d], consecutive threads load consecutive addresses if D is large... wait, no. Q is laid out as [N][D], so Q[0][d], Q[1][d] are D floats apart. That's a stride of D*4 = 4096 bytes. That's terrible for coalescing! Wait, the layout is [B, H, N, D]. So for a fixed b and h, the data for query q starts at offset q*D. Query q+1 is at (q+1)*D. So Q[q][d] and Q[q+1][d] are separated by D elements = D*4 bytes = 4096 bytes. A warp of 32 threads accessing Q[0][d], Q[1][d], ..., Q[31][d] has a stride of 4096 bytes between consecutive threads. That's NOT coalesced. Each thread in the warp accesses a different 128B cache line (4096/128 = 32 lines apart). Each warp transaction needs to fetch 32 cache lines = 4096 bytes. That's the worst possible pattern. This is a CRITICAL realization. For attention where each thread handles one query, we need the Q, K, V access pattern to be coalesced. To access Q coalesced, threads in a warp should access the same query's consecutive elements, or different elements of the SAME query. If a warp of 32 threads processes ONE query together, then they access Q[q][d+tid], which is perfectly coalesced. That's the flash attention style: one warp or block of warps processes a tile of queries, and threads within the tile access different D elements of the SAME query or queries. In my original kernel, I had a block processing BQ=8 queries, and threads collectively loaded Q[0..7][d] with coalesced accesses. That part was actually better. So the single-thread-per-query approach fails on Q coalescing. We need thread cooperation within queries. Back to the original kernel style, but optimized: - A block of threads cooperates to process BQ queries. - Threads in a warp access the same query or different D elements. Actually, the original kernel had: ```cpp for (int i = tid; i < BQ * DT; i += blockDim.x) { int q = i / DT; int d = i % DT; smem_q[q][d] = Q[head_offset + q_idx * D + dt + d]; } ``` This is coalesced because consecutive threads load consecutive memory addresses (outer loop over BQ*DT in thread-index-linear order, and memory is laid out as [N][D], so q_idx*D + dt + d are consecutive when d increments). Load V[k][t*32:(t+1)*32]. b. Broadcast weights via shuffle. c. Accumulate to O. This is actually a very clean approach! Let me formalize: Each warp handles 1 query. 1 block = 32 warps = 32 queries. Grid = (32 heads * 32 batches * 16 query_groups) = 16384 blocks. Wait, 512 queries / 32 queries per block = 16 blocks per head. Total blocks = 32 * 32 * 16 = 16384. Algorithm per warp (query q): ```cpp // Load Q into shared or local memory float q_local[32]; // 32 floats per thread for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) { q_local[i] = Q[q * D + threadIdx.x * 32 + i]; // thread t loads elements [t*32, (t+1)*32) } // Wait, threadIdx.x is 0..31 for warp 0? But a block has 32 warps. // threadIdx.x % 32 = lane_id // We can load: q_local[i] = Q[q*D + lane_id*32 + i]; ``` For score computation: For each key k = 0..511: float dot = 0; for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) { float k_val = K[k*D + lane_id*32 + i]; // same pattern as Q dot += q_local[i] * k_val; } // warp sum #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) dot += __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, dot, offset); dot *= scale; // update max and sum // store dot in local array? We need all 512 scores. ``` For 512 scores, storing in local memory: 512 floats = 2KB per thread. Local memory is global-backed and coalesced if laid out nicely. But 512 scores * 32 threads per warp = 64KB per warp. For 32 warps = 2MB per block. That's the same order as O output, so local memory spill might be OK. But actually, we can do online softmax WITHOUT storing all scores! The trick: process keys in groups, compute tile max, update running max, compute exp relative to tile max, accumulate to sum. For online softmax, we need to know the max to compute exp. If we process one key at a time: ```cpp float m = -inf; float l = 0; float o_local[32] = {0}; for (int k = 0; k < N; ++k) { float s = 0; for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) { s += q_local[i] * K[k*D + lane_id*32 + i]; } warp_reduce(s); s *= scale; float new_m = fmaxf(m, s); float corr = expf(m - new_m); float p = expf(s - new_m); l = l * corr + p; for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) { o_local[i] = o_local[i] * corr + p * V[k*D + lane_id*32 + i]; } m = new_m; } ``` Wait! This is BRILLIANT! With warp-level online softmax, each warp processes ONE query. All 32 threads in the warp cooperate: - Each thread handles a 32-dim chunk of Q, K, V. - The score is computed as a warp reduction. - The output is accumulated in each thread's 32-dim local accumulator. - No shared memory needed! - No need to store scores! Let me verify the algorithm carefully: 1. Thread t loads Q[q][t*32:(t+1)*32] into 32 registers. 2. For each key k: a. Thread t loads K[k][t*32:(t+1)*32] into 32 registers (or directly use). b. Thread t computes partial dot product: sum_i Q[i] * K[i] for its 32 dims. c. Warp reduce across 32 threads to get full score. d. Apply scale. e. `new_m = max(m, score)` f. `corr = exp(m - new_m)` g. `p = exp(score - new_m)` h. `l = l * corr + p` (but we don't actually need l if we keep unnormalized O) Wait, we DO need l for the final normalization. Or do we? Actually, with the standard online softmax formulation: ``` O_new = O_old * exp(m_old - m_new) + exp(s - m_new) * V l_new = l_old * exp(m_old - m_new) + exp(s - m_new) ``` At the end, O_final = O_new / l_new. This is correct. i. Thread t loads V[k][t*32:(t+1)*32]. j. Thread t updates each output dim: `o_local[i] = o_local[i] * corr + p * v_local[i]` 3. After all keys: `o_local[i] /= l;` // wait, l is the sum of exp(s_i - m_final) Actually, O_new already has the exp(s_i - m_new) weights. We just need to divide by l_new. 4. Thread t writes O[q][t*32:(t+1)*32] = o_local. But wait, there's a subtle issue: `corr = exp(m - new_m)` is the same for all threads in the warp. We should broadcast it. And `p = exp(s - new_m)` is the same for all threads (since s is the same for the whole warp after reduction). We can broadcast p too. Let's trace through carefully: ```cpp float q_local[32]; // load Q for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) q_local[i] = Q[q*D + lane*32 + i]; float m = -1e20f; float l = 0.0f; float o_local[32] = {0}; for (int k = 0; k < N; ++k) { float dot = 0.0f; // load K chunk into k_local? We can load directly. for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) { float k_val = K[k*D + lane*32 + i]; dot += q_local[i] * k_val; } // reduce dot across warp #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) dot += __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, dot, offset); dot *= scale; // broadcast m and l? Actually all threads have the same m and l. // Wait, m and l are scalars, each thread keeps its own copy. // But they all update identically because dot is the same. float new_m = fmaxf(m, dot); float corr = expf(m - new_m); float p = expf(dot - new_m); l = l * corr + p; // update O accumulators for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) { float v_val = V[k*D + lane*32 + i]; o_local[i] = o_local[i] * corr + p * v_val; } m = new_m; } // normalize for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) { o_local[i] /= l; O[q*D + lane*32 + i] = o_local[i]; } ``` But wait, `m` and `l` are updated identically on all threads, but without synchronization. Is that OK? Let's see: - `dot` is the same on all threads after the warp shuffle reduction. - `new_m = fmaxf(m, dot)` where `m` started the same on all threads (and remains the same). - `corr = expf(m - new_m)` is the same on all threads. - `p = expf(dot - new_m)` is the same. - `l = l * corr + p` updates identically. - `m = new_m` updates identically. I need to be careful with numerical precision and correctness. ```cpp __global__ void attention_kernel( const float* __restrict__ Q, const float* __restrict__ K, const float* __restrict__ V, float* __restrict__ O, int B, int H, int N, int D) { int batch = blockIdx.x; int head = blockIdx.y; int q_group = blockIdx.z; int lane = threadIdx.x; int warp = threadIdx.y; int q = q_group * 32 + warp; if (q >= N) return; int head_offset = ((batch * H + head) * N) * D; int q_offset = head_offset + q * D; float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)D); // Load Q: 32 floats per thread float q_local[32]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) { q_local[i] = Q[q_offset + lane * 32 + i]; } float o_local[32] = {0.0f}; float m = -1e20f; float l = 0.0f; // Iterate over all keys for (int k = 0; k < N; ++k) { int k_offset = head_offset + k * D; // Compute dot product Q·K float dot = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) { float k_val = K[k_offset + lane * 32 + i]; dot += q_local[i] * k_val; } // Warp-level reduction #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { dot += __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, dot, offset); } dot *= scale; // Online softmax update float new_m = fmaxf(m, dot); float corr = expf(m - new_m); float p = expf(dot - new_m); // Load V and update output #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) { float v_val = V[k_offset + lane * 32 + i]; o_local[i] = o_local[i] * corr + p * v_val; } l = l * corr + p; m = new_m; } // Normalize and write output float norm = 1.0f / l; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) { O[q_offset + lane * 32 + i] = o_local[i] * norm; } } ``` Wait, I need to check something critical about this kernel. The issue: `l = l * corr + p`. This maintains the sum of exp(s_i - m_current). At the end, m_current = max over all keys, so l = sum exp(s_i - max). And we normalize by l. This is correct. But what about `corr = exp(m - new_m)`? If m = -inf initially, and new_m = dot for the first key: - corr = exp(-inf - dot) = 0 - Then o_local = o_local * 0 + p * v = p * v. - l = 0 + p = exp(dot - dot) = 1. This is correct. For the second key, if dot < m: - new_m = m (old max) - corr = exp(m - m) = 1 - p = exp(dot - m) - o_local = o_local + p * v - l = l + p Correct. If dot > m: - new_m = dot - corr = exp(m - dot) - p = exp(dot - dot) = 1 - o_local = o_local * corr + 1 * v - l = l * corr + 1 Correct. However, there's a subtle precision issue. The kernel code: ```cpp __global__ void fused_attention( const float* __restrict__ Q, const float* __restrict__ K, const float* __restrict__ V, float* __restrict__ O, int B, int H, int N, int D) { int batch = blockIdx.x; float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)D); // Load Q float4 q4[8]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) { q4[i] = reinterpret_cast<const float4*>(Q + q_offset)[lane + i * 32]; } float o_reg[32]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) o_reg[i] = 0.0f; float m = -1e20f; float l = 0.0f; for (int k = 0; k < N; ++k) { int k_offset = batch * stride + head * head_stride + k * D; // Compute dot product float4 k4[8]; float dot = 0.0f; Let me build this kernel: ```cpp __global__ void fused_attention_kernel( const float* __restrict__ Q, const float* __restrict__ K, const float* __restrict__ V, float* __restrict__ O, int B, int H, int N, int D) { int batch = blockIdx.x; int head = blockIdx.y; int q_group = blockIdx.z; int lane = threadIdx.x; int warp = threadIdx.y; int q = q_group * 32 + warp; if (q >= N) return; int stride = H * N * D; int head_stride = N * D; int q_offset = batch * stride + head * head_stride + q * D; float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)D); float o_reg[32]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) o_reg[i] = 0.0f; float m = -1e20f; float l = 0.0f; for (int k = 0; k < N; ++k) { int k_offset = batch * stride + head * head_stride + k * D; float dot = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) { float4 q4 = reinterpret_cast<const float4*>(Q + q_offset)[lane + i * 32]; float4 k4 = reinterpret_cast<const float4*>(K + k_offset)[lane + i * 32]; dot += q4.x * k4.x; dot += q4.y * k4.y; dot += q4.z * k4.z; dot += q4.w * k4.w; } #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { dot += __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, dot, offset); } dot *= scale; float new_m = fmaxf(m, dot); float corr = expf(m - new_m); float p = expf(dot - new_m); #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) { float4 v4 = reinterpret_cast<const float4*>(V + k_offset)[lane + i * 32]; o_reg[i*4+0] = o_reg[i*4+0] * corr + p * v4.x; o_reg[i*4+1] = o_reg[i*4+1] * corr + p * v4.y; o_reg[i*4+2] = o_reg[i*4+2] * corr + p * v4.z; o_reg[i*4+3] = o_reg[i*4+3] * corr + p * v4.w; } l = l * corr + p; m = new_m; } float inv_l = 1.0f / l; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) { float4 o4; o4.x = o_reg[i*4+0] * inv_l; o4.y = o_reg[i*4+1] * inv_l; o4.z = o_reg[i*4+2] * inv_l; o4.w = o_reg[i*4+3] * inv_l; reinterpret_cast<float4*>(O + q_offset)[lane + i * 32] = o4; } } ``` Wait, I realize there's a crucial issue: Q is loaded inside the K loop. Actually, I realize there might be an simpler issue: the CUDA warp shuffle with `__shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, dot, offset)` works across the warp. So the shuffle operates correctly within each warp. Wait, is that right? In CUDA, threads in a block are linearized as: `linear_tid = threadIdx.x + threadIdx.y * blockDim.x + threadIdx.z * blockDim.x * blockDim.y` Warps consist of 32 consecutive threads in this linearization. So threads (0..31, constant y, constant z) are in the same warp. Yes! But the warp shuffle operates on threads in the same warp. And within a warp, the lane ID is `linear_tid % 32 = threadIdx.x % 32`. Since `threadIdx.x` ranges 0..31, lane ID is exactly `threadIdx.x`. So `__shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, dot, offset)` correctly exchanges between threads with different `threadIdx.x` values within the same warp. And since `dot` is computed identically by all threads in the warp (they load different q and k but end up with different partial sums), the shuffle adds them up correctly. Perfect. Now for the kernel: ``` __global__ void attention_kernel(...) { int b = blockIdx.x; int h = blockIdx.y; int qg = blockIdx.z * BQ; // query group start int tid = threadIdx.x; int warp_id = tid / 32; int lane_id = tid % 32; int q_local = warp_id; // 0..7 int q = qg + q_local; if (q >= N) return; // head offset in global memory int base = ((b * H + h) * N) * D; int q_offset = base + q * D; // registers float o_reg[32]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) o_reg[i] = 0.0f; float m = -1e20f; float l = 0.0f; float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)D); __shared__ float smem_q[BQ][64 + 4]; __shared__ float smem_k[BK][64 + 4]; __shared__ float smem_v[BK][64 + 4]; __shared__ float smem_p[BQ][BK]; __shared__ float smem_m[BQ]; __shared__ float smem_l[BQ]; // if first warp, init smem_m and smem_l if (warp_id == 0) { if (lane_id < BQ) { smem_m[lane_id] = -1e20f; smem_l[lane_id] = 0.0f; } } __syncthreads(); // Pre-load Q to smem (or just process tile by tile) // Actually we need Q in registers per thread, not smem, since each warp handles one query // But we load Q to smem for cooperative loading then threads read for (int k_tile = 0; k_tile < N; k_tile += BK) { // Step 1: Compute scores for this key tile float score = 0.0f; for (int d_tile = 0; d_tile < D; d_tile += 64) { // Load Q tile: [8][64] // Warp w loads row w { int q_load = warp_id; int row_offset = qg + q_load; if (row_offset < N) { int gmem_q_base = base + row_offset * D + d_tile; int smem_q_row = q_load; // Each thread loads 2 floats (float2) for (int j = lane_id; j < 32; j += 32) { // j is the float2 index within the 64-float row // Actually we want each thread to load 2 floats, so 32 threads cover 64 floats float2 q2 = reinterpret_cast<const float2*>(Q + gmem_q_base)[j]; smem_q[smem_q_row][j*2 + 0] = q2.x; smem_q[smem_q_row][j*2 + 1] = q2.y; } } else { // zero fill for (int j = lane_id; j < 32; j += 32) { smem_q[q_load][j*2 + 0] = 0.0f; smem_q[q_load][j*2 + 1] = 0.0f; } } } // Load K tile: [32][64] // 8 warps, each warp loads 4 rows { int rows_per_warp = BK / 8; // 4 for (int r = 0; r < rows_per_warp; ++r) { int k_load = warp_id * rows_per_warp + r; if (k_tile + k_load < N) { int gmem_k_base = base + (k_tile + k_load) * D + d_tile; int smem_k_row = k_load; for (int j = lane_id; j < 32; j += 32) { float2 k2 = reinterpret_cast<const float2*>(K + gmem_k_base)[j]; smem_k[smem_k_row][j*2 + 0] = k2.x; smem_k[smem_k_row][j*2 + 1] = k2.y; } } else { for (int j = lane_id; j < 32; j += 32) { smem_k[k_load][j*2 + 0] = 0.0f; smem_k[k_load][j*2 + 1] = 0.0f; } } } } __syncthreads(); // Compute dot product: my query vs my key int my_k = lane_id; // key within this tile if (k_tile + my_k < N) { #pragma unroll for (int d = 0; d < 64; ++d) { score += smem_q[q_local][d] * smem_k[my_k][d]; } } __syncthreads(); } score *= scale; // Step 2: Online softmax for this tile float my_s = score; float m_tile = my_s; // warp max #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { m_tile = fmaxf(m_tile, __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, m_tile, offset)); } // load previous m, l from smem float m_prev, l_prev; if (lane_id == 0) { m_prev = smem_m[q_local]; l_prev = smem_l[q_local]; } m_prev = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, m_prev, 0); l_prev = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, l_prev, 0); float m_new = fmaxf(m_prev, m_tile); For the O update with V in smem_v[BK][BD+pad]: ``` for (int k = 0; k < BK; ++k) { float p = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, my_p, k); if (d0 < D) o_reg[slot0] += p * smem_v[k][lane_id]; if (d1 < D) o_reg[slot1] += p * smem_v[k][lane_id + 32]; } ``` Wait, but this accumulates without the corr_prev factor. We need to apply corr_prev after each key tile! In FlashAttention, O is updated as: ``` O_new = O_old * corr_prev + P_tile @ V_tile ``` Where P_tile @ V_tile is the matrix product for the current tile. We compute this as a block and add to O_old * corr_prev. So the update is: ``` for each d: sum = 0 for k in tile: sum += p[q][k] * V[k][d] O[q][d] = O[q][d] * corr_prev + sum ``` We can pre-multiply O by corr_prev before adding sum: ``` for each register slot: o_reg[slot] *= corr_prev // then add sum ``` Or we can do it in the loop: ``` o_reg[slot] = o_reg[slot] * corr_prev + sum ``` Either way. But we need to multiply ALL slots by corr_prev before adding the new sum. We can do: ``` #pragma unroll for (int g = 0; g < 32; ++g) { o_reg[g] *= corr_prev; } ``` before the V loop, or inline during the V loop (but that would multiply by corr_prev for each k, which is wrong). So we must pre-multiply or post-multiply correctly. Pre-multiply approach: ``` // After computing p values and before V update for (g = 0; g < 32; ++g) o_reg[g] *= corr_prev; // Then accumulate the new contribution for (k = 0; k < BK; ++k) { float p = __shfl_sync(..., k); o_reg[slot0] += p * smem_v[k][lane_id]; o_reg[slot1] += p * smem_v[k][lane_id + 32]; } ``` This is correct and clean. But wait, what about d1 = d_tile + lane_id + 32 exceeding D? We should check. For D=1024, d_tile ranges 0..960 in steps of 64. d1 = d_tile + lane_id + 32. Max d1 = 960 + 31 + 32 = 1023. For lane_id=31, d1 = 1023 which is valid (last index). But for a generic D that's not a multiple of 64, we might need padding. Let's assume D is a multiple of 64 (which 1024 is). Also, for N not a multiple of 32, we'd need the out-of-bounds handling. OK, let me now write the actual kernel code. I'll keep it clean and well-commented. Hmm, after all this analysis, let me just try something simpler and see if it compiles. The key insight is that PyTorch's sdpa is already heavily optimized, so my custom kernel might not beat it easily. But let's try. Actually, let me also consider using Tensor Cores! Let me write this kernel now, being very careful. Actually, I want to try something: use float4 for memory access where possible, and simplify the kernel to minimize register usage. Let me write the kernel: ```cpp #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <math.h> #define BQ 8 #define BK 64 #define BD 64 #define WARPS 8 #define THREADS 256 __global__ void attention_kernel( const float* __restrict__ Q, const float* __restrict__ K, const float* __restrict__ V, float* __restrict__ O, int B, int H, int N, int D) { int b = blockIdx.x; int h = blockIdx.y; int tid = threadIdx.x; int warp_id = tid / 32; int lane_id = tid % 32; int head_offset = ((b * H + h) * N) * D; float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)D); __shared__ float smem_q[BQ][BD + 4]; __shared__ float smem_k[BK][BD + 4]; __shared__ float smem_v[BK][BD + 4]; __shared__ float smem_m[BQ]; __shared__ float smem_l[BQ]; for (int qg = 0; qg < N; qg += BQ) { // Initialize O, m, l for this query group float o_reg[32]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) o_reg[i] = 0.0f; float m_reg = -1e20f; float l_reg = 0.0f; __syncthreads(); if (tid < BQ) { smem_m[tid] = -1e20f; smem_l[tid] = 0.0f; } __syncthreads(); for (int kt = 0; kt < N; kt += BK) { // Compute scores for this key tile float score = (qg + warp_id < N && kt + lane_id < N) ? 0.0f : -1e20f; for (int dt = 0; dt < D; dt += BD) { // Load Q tile for (int i = tid; i < BQ * BD; i += THREADS) { int q = i / BD; int d = i % BD; int q_idx = qg + q; smem_q[q][d] = (q_idx < N) ? Q[head_offset + q_idx * D + dt + d] : 0.0f; } // Load K tile for (int i = tid; i < BK * BD; i += THREADS) { int k = i / BD; int d = i % BD; int k_idx = kt + k; smem_k[k][d] = (k_idx < N) ? K[head_offset + k_idx * D + dt + d] : 0.0f; } __syncthreads(); // Compute partial score if (qg + warp_id < N && kt + lane_id < N) { #pragma unroll for (int d = 0; d < BD; ++d) { score += smem_q[warp_id][d] * smem_k[lane_id][d]; } } __syncthreads(); } score *= scale; // Online softmax float my_s = score; float m_tile = my_s; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { m_tile = fmaxf(m_tile, __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, m_tile, offset)); } float m_prev = m_reg; float m_new = fmaxf(m_prev, m_tile); float corr_prev = expf(m_prev - m_new); float corr_tile = expf(m_tile - m_new); float p_val = expf(my_s - m_new); float l_tile = p_val; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { l_tile += __shfl_xor_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, l_tile, offset); } float l_new = l_reg * corr_prev + l_tile * corr_tile; m_reg = m_new; l_reg = l_new; // Pre-multiply O by corr_prev #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < 32; ++i) { o_reg[i] *= corr_prev; } // Update O with P_tile @ V_tile for (int dt = 0; dt < D; dt += BD) { // Load V tile for (int i = tid; i < BK * BD; i += THREADS) { int k = i / BD; int d = i % BD; int k_idx = kt + k; smem_v[k][d] = (k_idx < N) ? V[head_offset + k_idx * D + dt + d] : 0.0f; } __syncthreads(); int d0 = dt + lane_id; int d1 = dt + lane_id + 32; int slot0 = d0 / 32; int slot1 = d1 / 32; float sum0 = 0.0f; float sum1 = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int k = 0; k < BK; ++k) { float p = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, p_val, k); if (kt + k < N) { sum0 += p * smem_v[k][lane_id]; sum1 += p * smem_v[k][lane_id + 32]; } } if (qg + warp_id < N) { if (d0 < D) o_reg[slot0] += sum0; if (d1 < D) o_reg[slot1] += sum1; } __syncthreads(); } } // Write out int q_idx = qg + warp_id; if (q_idx < N) { float inv_l = 1.0f / l_reg; #pragma unroll for (int g = 0; g < 32; ++g) { int d = lane_id + g * 32; if (d < D) { O[head_offset + q_idx * D + d] = o_reg[g] * inv_l; } } } __syncthreads(); } } ``` Wait, I see an issue: I'm using m_reg and l_reg as per-thread registers, but these need to be per-query (per-warp), not per-thread. Since all threads in a warp compute the same query, and they all compute the same m_new and l_new, having each thread keep its own m_reg and l_reg is fine as long as they all compute the same values. And they do, because the warp-level reductions ensure all lanes get the same result. But wait - m_reg and l_reg are initialized per-thread. V[head_offset + k_idx * D + dt + d] : 0.0f;\n }\n __syncthreads();\n\n if (valid_q) {\n int d0 = dt + lane_id;\n int d1 = dt + lane_id + 32;\n int slot0 = d0 >> 5;\n int slot1 = d1 >> 5;\n\n float sum0 = 0.0f;\n float sum1 = 0.0f;\n #pragma unroll\n for (int k = 0; k < BK; ++k) {\n float p = __shfl_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, p_val, k);\n sum0 += p * smem_v[k][lane_id];\n sum1 += p * smem_v[k][lane_id + 32];\n }\n if (d0 < D) o_reg[slot0] += sum0;\n if (d1 < D) o_reg[slot1] += sum1;\n }\n __syncthreads();\n }\n }\n\n int q_idx = qg + warp_id;\n if (q_idx < N) {\n float inv_l = 1.0f / l_reg;\n #pragma unroll\n for (int g = 0; g < 32; ++g) {\n int d = lane_id + (g << 5);\n if (d < D) {\n O[head_offset + q_idx * D + d] = o_reg[g] * inv_l;\n }\n }\n } else if (q_idx < N) {\n // For invalid but inside bounds, write zeros\n #pragma unroll\n for (int g = 0; g < 32; ++g) {\n int d = lane_id + (g << 5);\n if (d < D) {\n O[head_offset + q_idx * D + d] = 0.0f;\n }\n }\n }\n __syncthreads();\n }\n}\n\ntorch::Tensor forward(torch::Tensor Q, torch::Tensor K, torch::Tensor V) {\n auto O = torch::empty_like(Q);\n int B = Q.size(0);\n int H = Q.size(1);\n int N = Q.size(2);\n int D = Q.size(3);\n dim3 grid(B, H);\n dim3 block(THREADS);\n attention_kernel<<<grid, block>>>(\n Q.data_ptr<float>(), K.data_ptr<float>(), V.data_ptr<float>(),\n O.data_ptr<float>(), B, H, N, D);\n return O;\n}\n'''\n\nfused_attention = load_inline(\n name=\"fused_attention_v3\",\n cpp_sources=\"torch::Tensor forward(torch::Tensor Q, torch::Tensor K, torch::Tensor V);\",\n cuda_sources=cuda_source,\n functions=[\"forward\"],\n extra_cuda_cflags=[\"-O3\", \"--use_fast_math\"],\n verbose=False,\n)\n\nclass ModelNew(nn.Module):\n def __init__(self):\n super(ModelNew, self).__init__()\n\n def forward(self, Q: torch.Tensor, K: torch.Tensor, V: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:\n Q = Q.contiguous()\n K = K.contiguous()\n V = V.contiguous()\n return fused_attention.forward(Q, K, V)\n\nif __name__ == \"__main__\":\n pass\n" }
